<div id="review_569301115" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/569301115" />
    <a title="Louisa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10378346-louisa"><img alt="Louisa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386310441p2/10378346.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/569301115?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Louisa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Louisa" href="/user/show/10378346-louisa">Louisa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780307975645" href="/book/show/17456790-two-boys-kissing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10378346-louisa?shelf=2013-favourites">2013-favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10378346-louisa?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10378346-louisa?shelf=favourite-ya">favourite-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10378346-louisa?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10378346-louisa?shelf=2013-read">2013-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10378346-louisa?shelf=coming-of-age">coming-of-age</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer569301115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12931188661259631082">I'd give this book a standing ovation if I could. Absolutely beautiful, life-affirming, and a story so needed amidst today's changing viewpoints on LGBT rights.<br/><br/>The cover and the title pretty much say it all. <i>Two Boys Kissing</i> runs the gamut of eight "main" characters - ex-boyfriends Craig and Harry aiming to break the Guinness World Record for longest kiss; Tariq, quasi-inspiration of the big kiss after getting beaten up by haters and staunch supporter of their challenge; steady couple Neil and P</span>
  <span id="freeText12931188661259631082" style="display:none">I'd give this book a standing ovation if I could. Absolutely beautiful, life-affirming, and a story so needed amidst today's changing viewpoints on LGBT rights.<br /><br />The cover and the title pretty much say it all. <i>Two Boys Kissing</i> runs the gamut of eight "main" characters - ex-boyfriends Craig and Harry aiming to break the Guinness World Record for longest kiss; Tariq, quasi-inspiration of the big kiss after getting beaten up by haters and staunch supporter of their challenge; steady couple Neil and Peter; pink-haired Avery born in a girl's body; blue-haired Ryan, the new boy Avery meets and boyfriend in the making; and Cooper, depressed by his identity and unable to live under the eventual weight of his family's disapproval. The reader experiences what it's like to be gay in America from several angles. It's both extremely hopeful and sad.<br /><br />The writing is also as gorgeous and raw as ever, peppered with quotes like these:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>We gather the things we learned, and they don't nearly add up to fill the space of a life. You will miss the taste of Froot Loops. You will miss the sound of traffic. You will miss your back against his. You will miss him stealing the sheets. <br /><br />Do not ignore these things.</i>
</blockquote><br /><br />People could not be reading this at a better time. Who can forget the Supreme Court's DOMA decision earlier in the year? I had the privilege of watching the D.C. Gay Pride Parade this June, and was totally overwhelmed in a fantastic way. Witnessing men openly celebrate their love for other men, women for women, etc. without fear of being lynched was truly lovely. But even as we celebrate a new age of same-sex rights, it's still worth knowing how "taboo" it is to certain people or cultures - Russia, for example, or even my own country, where almost no recognition is given to same-sex couples, and the conservative Asian mindset prevails.<br /><br />David Levithan has long been one of my favourite YA authors, even when I know, subconsciously, that he writes somewhat pretentiously. <i>Two Boys Kissing</i> feels a little preachy at times, too. <i>And</i> it's narrated by a Greek chorus of gay men who succumbed to AIDS many years ago. I can see readers being potentially put off by these factors. Personally, I don't see how they should dissuade one from reading what will probably become a defining novel in LGBT and YA literature. D Lev. himself is a gay man who wrote <i>Boy Meets Boy</i> just ten years ago, but realising how far LGBT rights have progressed since then is a revelation unto itself.<br /><br />There is always hope for a world in which one of my close friends can be open about his sexual identity without facing recrimination from his friends or family. I choose to believe it'll happen someday. If books like Levithan's could change the world, what a time to be alive.<br /><br />P.S. Check out <i>Will Grayson, Will Grayson</i> and <i>The Realm of Possibility</i> if you haven't either! Goddamn it, D Lev, you're good.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12931188661259631082" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2266279744" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2266279744" />
    <a title="Bianca" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29843800-bianca"><img alt="Bianca" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589154116p2/29843800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2266279744?book_show_action=true">Jan 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bianca" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bianca" href="/user/show/29843800-bianca">Bianca</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781405264433" href="/book/show/20453480-two-boys-kissing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=lgbtiq">lgbtiq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=literary-fiction">literary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=male-author">male-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=alternate-povs">alternate-povs</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29843800-bianca?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2266279744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16353082057489072411"><b>OMG! OMG! OMG!<br/></b><br/>This book ...<br/>How do I convey how good this book is, when I'm shouting expletives in my head- the kinds that express incredulity at having one's mind blown away. I'm also very sleep deprived, thanks to staying up late to finish it. So, bear with me.<br/><br/>I was browsing through 700+ books on my Kindle, to see if anything jumps at me, hoping for a book that wasn't blah. Honestly, I couldn't remember why I bought this book, especially since I had been thinking "I've about had enough of readi</span>
  <span id="freeText16353082057489072411" style="display:none"><b>OMG! OMG! OMG!<br /></b><br />This book ...<br />How do I convey how good this book is, when I'm shouting expletives in my head- the kinds that express incredulity at having one's mind blown away. I'm also very sleep deprived, thanks to staying up late to finish it. So, bear with me.<br /><br />I was browsing through 700+ books on my Kindle, to see if anything jumps at me, hoping for a book that wasn't blah. Honestly, I couldn't remember why I bought this book, especially since I had been thinking "I've about had enough of reading books about gay men ..."(to clarify, I've nothing against gay people, I just realised there are a lot of books with male gay characters and very few with lesbians and the feminist in me has an issue with it, as in not even the females in the gay community have equal representation etc. Don't mind me.) <br />I thought I'll just read a little bit and decide quickly if I continue or not. I was entrapped from the very beginning. <br /><br />The writing is out of this world. Every single sentence. Every single phrase. Nothing is superfluous.<br />The voice and the structure blew me away. You see, there's an omniscient narrator represinting the collective of gay men who'd passed away due to AIDS. They're looking at the younger gay generation - the Internet generation - contemplating, comparing, contrasting, advising from above. You see, they'd been through a lot, they had it rougher; things have improved, after all, two boys are kissing on a high school lawn, trying to beat the world record for the longest kiss and it's quite the record - <i>thirty-two hours, twelve minutes and ten seconds. </i> <br /><br />While things have improved, it's not all smooth sailing for the gay teenagers. We get an appreciation of the type of hurdles encountered via several characters' stories.<br /><br />The two boys kissing used to be a couple but they broke it off choosing to be just friends. Harry Ramirez is out, his parents are very supportive. Craig Cole has not come out to his parents yet.<br /><br />Then there's Tariq, a black gay teenager, who loves to dance. He was bashed one night, so he's a bit traumatised.<br /><br />Then there are the pink-haired boy, Avery, and the blue-haired boy, Ryan, who hit it off at a gay prom. Avery is a boy born in the wrong body. <br /><br />The saddest and most heartwrenching story is that of Cooper, who is in the closet, spends numerous hours trawling the Internet and the sex apps, pretending to be different people - characters, messing with people. He feels empty, lonely and he loathes himself.<br /><br />Levithan paints a pretty complex picture of what it is to be gay these days (well, the story is set in the 2013), especially for those living in a small town. He's gay himself so he knows what he's talking about. He also knows what the previous generations had to endure.<br /><br />This is a beautifully crafted, original novel. <br />I'm not American, I'm not a gay teenager, I had absolutely nothing in common with anything or anyone in this novel. Great writing makes one empathise, understand and learn. Levithan accomplished to do that and more.<br /><br />As far as I'm concerned <i>Two Boys Kissing</i> was PERFECT. Dare I say a masterpiece? Can we say that about a YA contemporary novel? I don't care. This is going straight to my <i>Favourites Shelf</i>.<br /><br />What a novel!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16353082057489072411" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer3461253712732398028">Loved it! I loved that the story was narrated by gay men who have passed away. It gives the story so much extra meaning. <br/><br/>Here are some quotes that, for me, packed a punch:<br/><br/>"***** fell to the ground, remembered someone telling him to curl up, to protect himself that way. They were laughing now, enjoying it, thrilled by it. He couldn't even yell for help, because the only sounds he could make were ones he'd never heard before, a wailing, gutteral acknowledgement of the sudden, intense pain as they </span>
  <span id="freeText3461253712732398028" style="display:none">Loved it! I loved that the story was narrated by gay men who have passed away. It gives the story so much extra meaning. <br /><br />Here are some quotes that, for me, packed a punch:<br /><br />"***** fell to the ground, remembered someone telling him to curl up, to protect himself that way. They were laughing now, enjoying it, thrilled by it. He couldn't even yell for help, because the only sounds he could make were ones he'd never heard before, a wailing, gutteral acknowledgement of the sudden, intense pain as they punched and they kicked, laughing their faggots at him as they broke his ribs."<br /> <br /> (I left the character's name out in case you haven't read the book yet.)<br /><br />"The first sentence of the truth is always the hardest. Each of us had a first sentence, and most of us found the strength to say it out loud to someone who deserved to hear it. What we hoped, and what we found, was that the second sentence of the truth is always easier than the first, and the third sentence is even easier than that. Suddenly you are speaking the truth in paragraphs, in pages. The fear, the nervousness, is still there, but it is joined by a new confidence. All along, you've used the first sentence as a lock. But now you find that it's the key."<br /><br /> (How true in anyone's life or circumstances. Also, no one should have to be afraid to tell people who they love. Hopefully that day will come.)<br /><br />"Not everything needs to be said at once. Sharing truth is not the kind of gift that comes in wrapping paper - ripped open at once and, there, you're done. No, this is a gift that must be unfolded. It is enough to start the telling. It's enough to have the beginning and feel like it's a beginning."<br /><br /> (Here the author is talking about first meeting a potential partner in life. I had to kind of chuckle cuz I am reminded of people you first meet, whether it's potential lovers, friends, or even strangers who give you their life story when all that's necessary is a hello, nice to meet you.....)<br /><br />"One of the kids who asks to pitch in is eleven years old. His name is Max, and his dad brought him to see this. Max is a marvel to us. He will never have to come out because he will never have been kept in. Even though he has a mom and a dad, they made sure from the beginning to tell him that it didn't have to be a mom and a dad. It could be a mom and a mom, a dad and a dad, just a mom, or just a dad. When Max's early affections become clear, he didn't think twice about them. He doesn't see it as defining him. It is just a part of his definition." <br /><br />"Some of our parents were always on our side. Some of our parents chose to banish us rather than see us for who we were. And some of our parents, when they found out we were sick, stopped being dragons and became dragonslayers instead. Sometimes that's what it takes - the final battle. But it should take much, much less than that."<br /><br />"The minute you stop talking about individuals and start talking about a group, your judgement has a flaw in it." <br /><br /> (How true is that sentence in the world we live in today especially!)<br /><br />I am not always a fan of YA but this one is great!!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1090440463" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1090440463" />
    <a title="Chris Horsefield" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14058695-chris-horsefield"><img alt="Chris Horsefield" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499793325p2/14058695.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1090440463?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Horsefield" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Horsefield" href="/user/show/14058695-chris-horsefield">Chris Horsefield</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1090440463" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4499646735760694300">Don't be put off - by the blurb and the kind of silly sounding story of two kids trying to break a world kissing record (barf) ad that's like saying Great Expectations is about a woman who's ruined a wedding cake…it's so much more than the initial premise.<br/>The two boys who are attempting the world record for kissing are the lynchpins of the story and the way that Harry and Craig communicate and support each other throughout their marathon is really touching. The reactions of the people around the</span>
  <span id="freeText4499646735760694300" style="display:none">Don't be put off - by the blurb and the kind of silly sounding story of two kids trying to break a world kissing record (barf) ad that's like saying Great Expectations is about a woman who's ruined a wedding cake…it's so much more than the initial premise.<br />The two boys who are attempting the world record for kissing are the lynchpins of the story and the way that Harry and Craig communicate and support each other throughout their marathon is really touching. The reactions of the people around them was both uplifting and saddening, but all the while they continued to support each other, without words, just with actions and it really made me feel that they were completely dedicated to their cause and each other.<br /><br />However, Two Boys Kissing is not just the story of Harry and Craig, it is also the story of several other boys that are drawn to Harry and Craigs world record attempt, all whilst experiencing their own life-changing and affirming situations. Two Boys Kissing doesn't have distinct chapter POVs, instead it flickers through the boys' stories, giving in depth views to their lives or brief flashes of life-changing moments. All the characters are three dimensional and so likeable, and I was drawn into all their stories as they struggled with their own identities, the pressures of their families and for acceptance from the people around them.<br /><br />I particularly loved Ryan and Avery who meet at the beginning of the story and navigate a multitude of issues whilst just trying to get to know each other. Levithan tells their story with sensitivity without resorting to sappy ways to grab sympathy, and I loved the way he protrayed their relationship.<br /><br />The one thing I was unsure of before I started reading was the Greek Chorus - I couldn't quite imagine how Levithan would pull it off, but he definitely proved me wrong. More than any of the individual characters, I was completely entranced by the Greek Chorus - and at times I felt quite emotional at their descriptions of their lives, struggles and the advice that they wanted to give all the teen boys that they were watching over. Having an emotional connection to nameless, faceless characters isn't something that happens often, and really shows just how talented David Levithan is as a writer.<br /><br />Two Boys Kissing is just another example of why I love David Levithan's writing and storytelling so much - although this is a short book, I was dreading the ending within the first 10 pages, and I had to force myself to read it slowly, so I could enjoy it for what it is - a wonderful, heartfelt YA GLBT novel that made me happy, sad, angry and hopeful all at the same time.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4499646735760694300" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12620745-debbie-dj?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12620745-debbie-dj?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>,

<span id="freeTextContainer4954434741793400131">HOLY MOLY! This made my all time favorites list!<br/><br/>I never would have thought with a title of “Two Boys Kissing,” and a not so great cover, I would have loved this book so much. Also, I get a little perturbed when it’s always boys and not girls. But, this this is so universal it didn’t matter.<br/><br/>Levithan centers his novel around a true event, two boys kissing to break a world record. But, my oh my, the narrators are the previous generation of gay men, looking down with support, understanding, and even</span>
  <span id="freeText4954434741793400131" style="display:none">HOLY MOLY! This made my all time favorites list!<br /><br />I never would have thought with a title of “Two Boys Kissing,” and a not so great cover, I would have loved this book so much. Also, I get a little perturbed when it’s always boys and not girls. But, this this is so universal it didn’t matter.<br /><br />Levithan centers his novel around a true event, two boys kissing to break a world record. But, my oh my, the narrators are the previous generation of gay men, looking down with support, understanding, and even resentment.<br /><br />I loved this early quote...<br />“We were once the ones living and then we were the ones dying. We sewed outfits, a thread’s width into your history. We were once like you, only our world wasn’t like yours. You have no idea how close to death you came. A generation or two earlier, you might be here with us. We resent you. You astonish us.”<br /><br />And, just OMG with the characters. Two boys meet at a gay prom (not in my day!) Two others are trying to negotiate a relationship, another has been assaulted, and one appears damaged beyond repair by his parents lack of acceptance. While this may be a YA book, the writing was phenomenal!<br /><br />Personally I could relate to so many of the characters struggles as many of my own were painful. So yes, this book made me cry, but also filled me with hope. While this is about the gay experience, it also reminded me about the struggles of immigrants, Native Americans, African Americans, etc. That’s why I found this book to be so universal. It was also a great reminder of the price paid by countless others who came before to ease the way. Yup, can’t recommend enough!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4954434741793400131" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer16984259376586516319"><b>4 Stars!</b><br/><br/>Heartbreaking while uplifting, this was an unique tale showcasing the challenges the LGBT community faced and still faces. <br/><br/>This chronicles a couple days in the life of several teens and their journey towards finding love and themselves, all told by the affecting omniscient and collective voices of those who’ve come before and are now long gone, tragically taken by AIDS. <br/><br/>While wistfully sad and bittersweet, this was full of hope and optimism and a recommended read!<br/><br/></span>

I feel that it's a must read for every age, but the fact that it's shelved in the YA section wa</span>
  <span id="freeText15508873155990851378" style="display:none">Two Boys Kissing is a powerful read. The story encompasses several stories of the struggles of what it means to be a gay youth all the while describing the joy and pain of trying to break the world's record for the longest kiss. Was that a run on sentence? I feel a little overwhelmed from just finishing this deeply emotional book. <br /><br />*cleansing breath* First of all, I'm delighted that this is a YA novel. I feel that it's a must read for every age, but the fact that it's shelved in the YA section warms my heart. Secondly, David Levithan is a master at writing about those who had died of AIDS as a background voice. It was kind of an ethereal feeling as I read. Tragic and poignant. I was touched by this novel and it has left a mark on my heart. We are born equal. Period.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2576027917" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2576027917" />
    <a title="Richard Derus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus"><img alt="Richard Derus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494992210p2/3920693.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2576027917?book_show_action=true">Nov 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard Derus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard Derus" href="/user/show/3920693-richard-derus">Richard Derus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3920693-richard-derus?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3920693-richard-derus?shelf=returned">returned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3920693-richard-derus?shelf=quiltbag">quiltbag</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2576027917" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2472538635294306419">Real Rating: 3.5* of five<br/><br/>Were I a teen, I'd be over the moon about this interlocking-loves narrative. I'm not, and I haven't been in a very very long time (<a href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nREV8bQJ1MA' rel='nofollow noopener'>the Bee Gees charted the last year of my teens</a>), so my muted response to the teen-angst "does he/doesn't he/will he/won't he" stuff is pretty much assured.<br/><br/>Others have commented on the dead gay men of my generation being the collective narrators with everything from tolerant smirks to outright derision. I am not a fan of second-person narratio</span>
  <span id="freeText2472538635294306419" style="display:none">Real Rating: 3.5* of five<br /><br />Were I a teen, I'd be over the moon about this interlocking-loves narrative. I'm not, and I haven't been in a very very long time (<a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=nREV8bQJ1MA" rel="nofollow noopener">the Bee Gees charted the last year of my teens</a>), so my muted response to the teen-angst "does he/doesn't he/will he/won't he" stuff is pretty much assured.<br /><br />Others have commented on the dead gay men of my generation being the collective narrators with everything from tolerant smirks to outright derision. I am not a fan of second-person narration. At All. However much I don't like that narrative choice, I do feel the acknowledgment of those gone before is a net positive choice. We, the AIDS generation, largely vanished after the disease decimated us because there weren't descendants or loving memories in families for far, far too many of us. Author Levithan doesn't hold with the vanishing of memory. He addresses this issue head-on and makes it a vibrant part of his narrative. This pleases me. I feel it as a chance for those gone to have The Talk with their spiritual descendants despite being incorporeal.<br /><br />So all the stars for including the ancestors in present-day life.<br /><br />But I'm old and cranky, so I'm retracting some stars for artificial inclusiveness. Not every point on the spectrum must needs be in every story. It could be my age showing (not a word, you) but it feels to me as though I'm being hectored. Again, not a teen, but as a teen I suspect I'd feel the same way. (Like I did about <i>The Outsiders</i>'s preachiness all those years ago.)<br /><br />Got a gay nephew? Cousin? Give him this book. Face down the outrage of the parents and show him he's not alone, not the first, and not bad/wrong/weird. I wish like hell this book had been around in 1972, instead of written by a man born then.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2472538635294306419" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer8276635596295126434"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/505817.gif' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><br/>When The Doctor asks, you don't refuse. <br/><br/><br/><b>After Finishing<br/><br/>3.5 Stars</b><br/><br/>Two Boys Kissing is not only a book about two boys. It follows the life of a long-time couple, a broken up couple, a new couple, and a boy searching to be part of a couple. <br/>Watching over these boys are the lost ones. The people we have lost from disease and suicide, the ones who look at these boys with both worry and envy, the ones of a lost generation of gay teenagers not unlike the ones we're reading about now. <br/><br/>I was looking forw</span>
  <span id="freeText8276635596295126434" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/505817.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>When The Doctor asks, you don't refuse. <br><br><br><b>After Finishing<br><br>3.5 Stars</b><br><br>Two Boys Kissing is not only a book about two boys. It follows the life of a long-time couple, a broken up couple, a new couple, and a boy searching to be part of a couple. <br>Watching over these boys are the lost ones. The people we have lost from disease and suicide, the ones who look at these boys with both worry and envy, the ones of a lost generation of gay teenagers not unlike the ones we're reading about now. <br><br>I was looking forward to this book a great deal. Kissing boys? A book with kissing boys on the cover? A book by David Levithan? Oh yes, yes, yes. <br>Unfortunately, it did not live up to the hype it is currently getting and it certainly didn't live up to his last book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13262783.Every_Day__Every_Day___1_" title="Every Day (Every Day, #1) by David Levithan" rel="nofollow noopener">Every Day</a>. <br><br>The first 70 pages were boring, erratically confusing, and trying far too hard to be profound and dramatic. <br>After that, it did get interesting but I never really got into the story.<br><br>The lack of chapters and the constant storyline switches were seriously irritating. I wish Levithan had left it to three perspectives instead of five, six, or seven. Because there were so many characters, I couldn't connect with any of them. Right when I was starting to get into one boy's story, it switched to another one. <br><br>Yes, the ending was very good and meaningful and more books should be made with gay characters as the <i>main</i> characters (instead of these half-assed 'random gay side characters' a lot of YA books feature nowadays).<br><br>But this book completely fails in the storytelling aspect, and that ultimately ruined it for me. </span>

<div id="review_791781675" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/791781675" />
    <a title="David Schaafsma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma"><img alt="David Schaafsma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574997804p2/269235.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/791781675?book_show_action=true">Oct 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Schaafsma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Schaafsma" href="/user/show/269235-david-schaafsma">David Schaafsma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=ya-fall-2018">ya-fall-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/269235-david-schaafsma?shelf=ya-glbt">ya-glbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer791781675" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14524181707847000725">David Levithan writes a YA novel that is both epistolary and hortatory, a letter of encouragement from one generation of dead gay men to the current generation of gay boys. It was inspired in part by a Walt Whitman poem where he misheard the first line as two boys kissing:<br/><br/>We two boys together clinging,	 <br/>One the other never leaving,	 <br/>Up and down the roads going—North and South excursions making,	 <br/>Power enjoying—elbows stretching—fingers clutching,	 <br/>Arm’d and fearless—eating, drinking, sleeping, l</span>
  <span id="freeText14524181707847000725" style="display:none">David Levithan writes a YA novel that is both epistolary and hortatory, a letter of encouragement from one generation of dead gay men to the current generation of gay boys. It was inspired in part by a Walt Whitman poem where he misheard the first line as two boys kissing:<br /><br />We two boys together clinging,	 <br />One the other never leaving,	 <br />Up and down the roads going—North and South excursions making,	 <br />Power enjoying—elbows stretching—fingers clutching,	 <br />Arm’d and fearless—eating, drinking, sleeping, loving,	 <br />No law less than ourselves owning—sailing, soldiering, thieving, threatening,	 <br />Misers, menials, priests alarming—air breathing, water drinking, <br />on the turf or the sea-beach dancing,<br />Cities wrenching, ease scorning, statutes mocking, feebleness chasing,	 <br />Fulfilling our foray.	<br /> <br />It was also inspired by an actual event, two boys trying to break the Guinness Book of World Record for a continuous kiss (more than 32 hours). A similar quest between two ex-boyfriends, Craig and Harry, is the spine of this book. What also happens (in the “guts” of the book) tacks back and forth between different stories of gay boys—an established couple, Peter and Neil; a new couple, Avery (who is also transsexual) and Ryan; and Cooper, alone and surfing chat rooms with fake identities. And Tariq, who is beaten up and films the (above) kiss.<br /><br />Maybe because I am a parent, I paid as much attention to how families supported or failed to support their sons:<br /><br />“It is hard to stop seeing your son as a son and to start seeing him as a human being. <br />It is hard to stop seeing your parents as parents and to start seeing them as human beings.<br />It's a two-sided transition, and very few people manage it gracefully.”<br /><br />“So many of us had to make our own families. So many of us had to pretend when we were home. So many of us had to leave. But every single one of us wishes we hadn’t had to. Every single one of us wishes our family had acted like our family, that even when we found a new family, we hadn’t had to leave the other one behind. Every single one of us would have loved to have been loved unconditionally by our parents.”<br /><br />When some families fail to support their sons in coming out (and I mean this in the book and in life), it is brutal and heartbreaking. When some local guys in the book fail to support the kissers or bully or beat up their gay peers, it is hard to read, and we are sadly still not surprised. There may be relatively safe places to be gay in this country, but we also know there is hatred to the point of violence in some places.<br /><br />I found the book inspiring, sometimes moving (okay, I cried 2-3 times, are you happy you made me tell?!), sometimes sad, and especially important to put in the hands (maybe especially) of gay boys. I found the gay collective plural third person hortatory approach a little hard to get engaged with and abstract, a bit too much telling and not enough showing/storying. A little meme-ish and preachy and unsurprising in places. But I like the various contemporary stories and I'm old enough to recall the worst horrors of the early onset of AIDS. This is a book that could not 20 years ago have been the publishing event it became. The cover I like, with two boys kissing, though I understand it has been controversial. Good! Be controversial, if you need to be, or rather, let the world stop making love in any form controversial.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14524181707847000725" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18231901049218559391">I have no words! This was absolutely amazing! I started it just a couple of hours ago and I couldn't put it down.   <span id="freeText18231901049218559391" style="display:none">I have no words! This was absolutely amazing! I started it just a couple of hours ago and I couldn't put it down. So mesmerising!<br /><br />I don't want to spoil the story, it's astonishing and I loved every single character, not only the "2 boys kissing", but also Avery and Ryan, Neil and Peter, even Cooper. They all broke my heart. I want to hug them all and keep them safe from any harm. Such wonderful souls! <br /><br />This is a book about dreams, aspirations, feelings, heart-breaking, hurting, hope, dead hope, broken dreams and everything in between and beyond!<br /><br />I've never loved a writing style more than I loved this author's. This was my first book by him, but it won't be the last. The writing is so flawless, so captivating. Why am I reading this book just now?! Everything written was so powerful! It makes you want to scream and yell and shake things! It also makes you want to change something in the world and be a better and more accepting person.<br /><br />I recommend this book to all my GR friends. It's one of those extraordinary books that you'll remember for a long time.<br /><br />On the final note, the author explains that he was inspired by the longest kiss between Matty and Bobby in 2010. I just saw it on YouTube and it is truly inspiring. I'm so glad there are people like them out there, brave and stoic. There is still hope!</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2271180082" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2271180082" />
    <a title="Cheri" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/106692-cheri"><img alt="Cheri" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1601402708p2/106692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2271180082?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cheri" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cheri" href="/user/show/106692-cheri">Cheri</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/18341484-two-boys-kissing">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=library-book">library-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/106692-cheri?shelf=lgbt">lgbt</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2271180082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3860481973357790393"><i>
  <b>“Does he love me, I want to know<br/>How can I tell if he loves me so<br/>“Is it in his eyes, oh no you'll be deceived<br/>Is it in his eyes, oh no you'll make believe<br/>If you want to know, if he loves you so<br/>It's in his kiss<br/>That's where it is, oh yeah”</b>
</i><br/>		“It’s in His Kiss” / ”The Shoop Shoop Song (It’s in His Kiss)” Songwriters: Rudy Clark <br/><br/>I remember seeing this title when I read another David Levithan book, <i>‘Dash & Lily’s Book of Dares’</i> and enjoying it so much that I wanted to check out some of his other boo</span>
  <span id="freeText3860481973357790393" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>“Does he love me, I want to know<br />How can I tell if he loves me so<br />“Is it in his eyes, oh no you'll be deceived<br />Is it in his eyes, oh no you'll make believe<br />If you want to know, if he loves you so<br />It's in his kiss<br />That's where it is, oh yeah”</b>
</i><br />		“It’s in His Kiss” / ”The Shoop Shoop Song (It’s in His Kiss)” Songwriters: Rudy Clark <br /><br />I remember seeing this title when I read another David Levithan book, <i>‘Dash &amp; Lily’s Book of Dares’</i> and enjoying it so much that I wanted to check out some of his other books. I remember seeing the cover, and title of this and thinking about the fact that this is a YA book, and the potential for it being too simplified, too trying-too-hard, too trendy, maybe.<br /><br />And then recently I ran across several of my goodreads friends reviews for this, as they had recently read this. I read Jaidee’s lovely review first, then Bianca’s, which had me add this, and then soon after followed Debbie’s review, which had me check my library for a copy, and (much to my surprise) then I had a copy to read. And then Larry’s review. <br /><br />What I loved about Dash &amp; Lilly’s story was that it was sweet, but told in a realistic way, and although it was aimed at a YA audience, it didn’t speak down to the intended audience.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>”You can’t know what it is like for us now—you will always be one step behind.<br />	Be thankful for that.<br />	You can’t know what it was like for us then—you will always be one step ahead. <br />	Be thankful for that, too.<br />	Trust us: There is a nearly perfect balance between the past and the future. As we become the distant past, you become a future few of us would have imagined.”</b>
</i><br /><br />Spoken by a chorus of men who died of AIDS, they are watching over the new generation who are still navigating who they are, where they fit in, who they can tell their secrets to, and who sees them as an abomination to be taunted, scorned. Pleas for help were ignored, their disease branded them, the world saw no need to save them, those who proclaimed themselves judge and jury sentenced these men to die. <br /><br />Alternating with the advice, love and wisdom projected by these men from beyond as these young gay men / boys are trying to navigate their way through life, navigate these murky waters of attraction in an environment that is sometimes accepting, sometimes hostile toward boys kissing boys.<br /><br />I loved this. <br /><br />Please check out these reviews, they’ve all said it much more eloquently, more glowingly, more thoroughly than I could ever hope to do. <br /><br />Jaidee’s review: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2084040315">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br />Bianca’s review:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2266279744">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br />Debbie’s review:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2268938969">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br />Larry’s review: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/705676049">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a><br /><br /><br />Many thanks, once again, to the Public Library system, and the many Librarians that manage, organize and keep it running, for the loan of this book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3860481973357790393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_601158500" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/601158500" />
    <a title="Thomas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas"><img alt="Thomas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1567953607p2/2018505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/601158500?book_show_action=true">Apr 27, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Thomas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Thomas" href="/user/show/2018505-thomas">Thomas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=lgbtq">lgbtq</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=realistic-fiction">realistic-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2018505-thomas?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer601158500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer249842173528058126"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>While I applaud David Levithan's ambition in writing a book like this, it did not blow me away. Even though <i>Two Boys Kissing</i> focuses on two boys staying connected - literally by the mouth - for more than 24 hours, I felt distanced from all of the characters in this novel.<br/><br/><i>Two Boys Kissing</i> revolves around Craig and Henry, two boys trying to set the record for longest kiss in the world. While they broke up before setting out on this mission, Peter and Neil are a couple, even though they ha</span>
  <span id="freeText249842173528058126" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />While I applaud David Levithan's ambition in writing a book like this, it did not blow me away. Even though <i>Two Boys Kissing</i> focuses on two boys staying connected - literally by the mouth - for more than 24 hours, I felt distanced from all of the characters in this novel.<br /><br /><i>Two Boys Kissing</i> revolves around Craig and Henry, two boys trying to set the record for longest kiss in the world. While they broke up before setting out on this mission, Peter and Neil are a couple, even though they have issues as well. Avery sets out on a new relationship with Ryan, hoping that his transgender status will not harm their new bond. And Cooper faces a tough journey after his father finds out about his homosexuality.<br /><br />The amount of characters detracted from the quality of this book the most. Levithan would write beautiful, meaningful passages but I would feel little emotion reading them, mainly because each character had so little space for development beyond his surface level features. It felt like the characters were vehicles for the deeper messages and the Greek chorus of dead men method of narration as opposed to actual, breathing people.<br /><br />Overall, a good read, and I am thankful that this book exists. I wholeheartedly support the themes and messages within the novel and I would recommend <i>Two Boys Kissing</i> to David Levithan fans as well as YA contemporary fiction fans searching for something different.</span>
  <a data-text-id="249842173528058126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2311684361" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2311684361" />
    <a title="Betsy Robinson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5149179-betsy-robinson"><img alt="Betsy Robinson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404493492p2/5149179.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2311684361?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Betsy Robinson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Betsy Robinson" href="/user/show/5149179-betsy-robinson">Betsy Robinson</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2311684361" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9654941601896186437">Almost from the first word, the writing pulls you into a vortex, swirling you through this story, told by a single-voiced chorus of dead gay men. Absolutely mesmerizing. <br/><br/>I owe Goodreaders Debbie Annan and Esil a great debt for their reviews. Never in a million years would I have gravitated to a Y.A. book with this cover and this title. But now that I have read the book, I understand the publisher's reasoning: to get this book to young gay boys and girls who need it. They did the right thing to r</span>
  <span id="freeText9654941601896186437" style="display:none">Almost from the first word, the writing pulls you into a vortex, swirling you through this story, told by a single-voiced chorus of dead gay men. Absolutely mesmerizing. <br><br>I owe Goodreaders Debbie Annan and Esil a great debt for their reviews. Never in a million years would I have gravitated to a Y.A. book with this cover and this title. But now that I have read the book, I understand the publisher's reasoning: to get this book to young gay boys and girls who need it. They did the right thing to reach them. But unfortunately it risks turning off a huge adult audience for such glorious literary writing. <br><br>Please don't be turned off!<br><br>The chorus of ancestors who intone this story feels like an archetypal entity that we humans are born to recognize. The Greeks used them, and when it is done honestly, it resonates in our bone marrow. I have this Sakti Burman lithograph hanging over my bed:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1520290721i/25167666.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>It speaks to my marrow this way.<br><br>But <i>Two Boys Kissing</i> is a specific story about being gay that anybody who lost friends during the government-ignored AIDS epidemic would appreciate in the most personal way. It threw me back in time to losing my friend and colleague Ron; I relived conferring with my remarkable work friend <a href="https://www.lgbtran.org/Profile.aspx?ID=3" rel="nofollow noopener">Bill Johnson</a> who was on the front lines of the crisis providing information to people with AIDS (this book prompted me to google him and find that link); I viscerally remembered seeing a performance of the <a href="http://www.nycgmc.org/our-history" rel="nofollow noopener">New York Gay Men's Chorus</a> whose positive energy exploded in the face of the epidemic; and then there was my experience with the valiant rebels of the <a href="http://www.nycgmc.org/our-history" rel="nofollow noopener">Gay Men's Health Center</a> who broke rules to take my donation of my dead mother's prescription drugs and assured me, yes, the Interferon would go free to anybody who needed it. All these AIDS warriors are represented in the riveting voice of the omniscient dead spirits who tell this story, and the sound vibrates through your heart.<br><br>This is mature, deep, transcendent storytelling. The words seem to invade your very cells as they spin off the page.<br><br>I wish they had published two different covers and done two separate runs to reach the two different audiences: gay kids and literary readers of all ages.<br><br><b>Update</b> <br>Just discovered there is another cover:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/books/1396280262l/20453480.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="9654941601896186437" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('OhB/OvCTRhju7kqu7sPzB8qM+GqpzpZS84BslROLj+n8xQoyg0T7u+g6abivJ5vLs31b8pWM/LEGSDP853UgIw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('aLeIpbtR9tcPDkPcxXMaGoqYpUhFD1qNsgpNNTno0ROuYv2tyIZLdAnaYMqEl3LW82kG0HlNMG5HwhJczRZ+2Q==')})
  }

          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('bookCover_33385229').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('bookCover_33385229').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();
            swapContent(lessLink);
          }
        });
      });

//]]>
</script>

</li>
</ul>
</div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1306981752081361032">David Levithan (born 1972) is an American children's book editor and award-winning author. He published his first YA book,<i> Boy Meets Boy</i>, in 2003. Levithan is also the founding editor of PUSH, a Young Adult imprint of Scholastic Press.<br/><br/></span>
